</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:H5N1_sidebar" title="Template:H5N1 sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template_talk:H5N1_sidebar" title="Template talk:H5N1 sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:H5N1_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_A" class="mw-redirect" title="Influenzavirus A">Influenzavirus A</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H5N1" class="mw-redirect" title="H5N1">H5N1</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transmission_and_infection_of_H5N1" title="Transmission and infection of H5N1">Transmission and infection of H5N1</a></div>
<p>Influenza infects many animal species, and transfer of viral strains between species can occur. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">Birds</a> are thought to be the main <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Host_(biology)" title="Host (biology)">animal reservoirs</a> of influenza viruses.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-273">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Most influenza strains are believed to have originated after humans began their intensive domestication of animals about 10,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-274">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Sixteen forms of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemagglutinin" title="Hemagglutinin">hemagglutinin</a> and nine forms of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuraminidase" title="Neuraminidase">neuraminidase</a> have been identified. All known subtypes (HxNy) are found in birds, but many subtypes are <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> in humans, dogs, horses, and pigs; populations of camels, ferrets, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cat" title="Cat">cats</a>, seals, mink, and whales also show evidence of prior infection or exposure to influenza.<sup id="cite_ref-webster_60-1" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-webster-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Variants of flu virus are sometimes named according to the species the strain is endemic in or adapted to. The main variants named using this convention are: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avian_influenza" title="Avian influenza">bird flu</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_flu" class="mw-redirect" title="Human flu">human flu</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swine_flu" class="mw-redirect" title="Swine flu">swine flu</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horse_flu" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse flu">horse flu</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dog_flu" class="mw-redirect" title="Dog flu">dog flu</a>. (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cat_flu" title="Cat flu">Cat flu</a> generally refers to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feline_viral_rhinotracheitis" title="Feline viral rhinotracheitis">feline viral rhinotracheitis</a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feline_calicivirus" title="Feline calicivirus">feline calicivirus</a> and not infection from an influenza virus.) In pigs, horses and dogs, influenza symptoms are similar to humans, with cough, fever and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anorexia_(symptom)" title="Anorexia (symptom)">loss of appetite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-webster_60-2" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-webster-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The frequency of animal diseases are not as well-studied as human infection, but an outbreak of influenza in harbor seals caused approximately 500 seal deaths off the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> coast in 1979–1980.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-275">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> However, outbreaks in pigs are common and do not cause severe mortality.<sup id="cite_ref-webster_60-3" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-webster-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_vaccine" title="Influenza vaccine">Vaccines</a> have also been developed to protect poultry from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avian_influenza" title="Avian influenza">avian influenza</a>. These vaccines can be effective against multiple strains and are used either as part of a preventive strategy, or combined with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culling" title="Culling">culling</a> in attempts to eradicate outbreaks.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-276">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bird_flu">Bird flu</span></h3>
<p>Flu symptoms in birds are variable and can be unspecific.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-277">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> The symptoms following infection with low-pathogenicity avian influenza may be as mild as ruffled feathers, a small reduction in egg production, or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weight_loss" title="Weight loss">weight loss</a> combined with minor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respiratory_disease" title="Respiratory disease">respiratory disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-278">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> Since these mild symptoms can make diagnosis in the field difficult, tracking the spread of avian influenza requires laboratory testing of samples from infected birds. Some strains such as Asian <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H9N2" class="mw-redirect" title="H9N2">H9N2</a> are highly virulent to poultry and may cause more extreme symptoms and significant mortality.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-279">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> In its most highly pathogenic form, influenza in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chickens</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">turkeys</a> produces a sudden appearance of severe symptoms and almost 100% mortality within two days.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-280">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> As the virus spreads rapidly in the crowded conditions seen in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">intensive farming</a> of chickens and turkeys, these outbreaks can cause large economic losses to poultry farmers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>An avian-adapted, highly pathogenic strain of H5N1 (called HPAI A(H5N1), for "highly pathogenic avian influenza virus of type A of subtype H5N1") causes <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transmission_and_infection_of_H5N1" title="Transmission and infection of H5N1">H5N1 flu</a>, commonly known as "avian influenza" or simply "bird flu", and is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemic_(epidemiology)" title="Endemic (epidemiology)">endemic</a> in many bird populations, especially in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. This Asian lineage strain of HPAI A(H5N1) is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_spread_of_H5N1" title="Global spread of H5N1">spreading globally</a>. It is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epizootic" title="Epizootic">epizootic</a> (an epidemic in non-humans) and panzootic (a disease affecting animals of many species, especially over a wide area), killing tens of millions of birds and spurring the culling of hundreds of millions of other birds in an attempt to control its spread. Most references in the media to "bird flu" and most references to H5N1 are about this specific strain.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-281">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-282">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>HPAI A(H5N1) is an avian disease and there is no evidence suggesting efficient human-to-human transmission of HPAI A(H5N1). In almost all cases, those infected have had extensive physical contact with infected birds.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-283">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> H5N1 may mutate or reassort into a strain capable of efficient human-to-human transmission. The exact changes that are required for this to happen are not well understood.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-284">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> Due to the high lethality and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virulence" title="Virulence">virulence</a> of H5N1, its <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemic_(epidemiology)" title="Endemic (epidemiology)">endemic</a> presence, and its large and increasing biological host reservoir, the H5N1 virus was the world's major pandemic threat in the 2006–07 flu season, and billions of dollars are being raised and spent researching H5N1 and preparing for a potential influenza pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_258-1" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-Rosenthal-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ChineseFluInspectors.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/ChineseFluInspectors.JPG/170px-ChineseFluInspectors.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/ChineseFluInspectors.JPG/255px-ChineseFluInspectors.JPG 1.5x, https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/ChineseFluInspectors.JPG/340px-ChineseFluInspectors.JPG 2x" data-file-width="441" data-file-height="443" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ChineseFluInspectors.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chinese inspectors checking airline passengers for fevers, a common symptom of swine flu</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2013, the Chinese government reported three cases of H7N9 influenza infections in humans, two of whom had died and the third became critically ill. Although the strain of the virus is not thought to spread efficiently between humans,<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-285">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-286">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> by mid-April, at least 82 persons had become ill from H7N9, of which 17 had died. These cases include three small family clusters in Shanghai and one cluster between a neighboring girl and boy in Beijing, raising at least the possibility of human-to-human transmission. The WHO points out that one cluster did not have two of the cases lab confirmed and further points out, as a matter of baseline information, that some viruses are able to cause limited human-to-human transmission under conditions of close contact but are not transmissible enough to cause large community outbreaks.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-287">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-288">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WHO_H7N9_289-0" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-WHO_H7N9-289">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swine_flu">Swine flu</span></h3>
<p>In pigs <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swine_influenza" title="Swine influenza">swine influenza</a> produces fever, lethargy, sneezing, coughing, difficulty breathing and decreased appetite.<sup id="cite_ref-Kothalawala_290-0" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-Kothalawala-290">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> In some cases the infection can cause abortion. Although mortality is usually low, the virus can produce weight loss and poor growth, causing economic loss to farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-Kothalawala_290-1" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-Kothalawala-290">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> Infected pigs can lose up to 12 pounds of body weight over a three- to four-week period.<sup id="cite_ref-Kothalawala_290-2" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-Kothalawala-290">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> Direct transmission of an influenza virus from pigs to humans is occasionally possible (this is called <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoonosis" title="Zoonosis">zoonotic</a> swine flu). In all, 50 human cases are known to have occurred since the virus was identified in the mid-20th century, which have resulted in six deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-Myers_291-0" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-Myers-291">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, a swine-origin <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H1N1" class="mw-redirect" title="H1N1">H1N1</a> virus strain commonly referred to as "swine flu" caused the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 flu pandemic">2009 flu pandemic</a>, but there is no evidence that it is endemic to pigs (i.e. actually a swine flu) or of transmission from pigs to people; instead, the virus spreads from person to person.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-292">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-293">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> This strain is a reassortment of several strains of H1N1 that are usually found separately, in humans, birds, and pigs.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="Influenza#cite_note-294">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-CDC2014Key-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-CDC2014Key_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-CDC2014Key_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-CDC2014Key_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-CDC2014Key_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cdc.gov/flu/about/keyfacts.htm">"Key Facts About Influenza (Flu)"</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC). 9 September 2014. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141202191706/https://www.cdc.gov/flu/keyfacts.htm">Archived</a> from the original on 2 December 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. </li>
<li id="cite_note-Einav2020-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-Einav2020_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-Einav2020_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-Einav2020_6-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFEinavGentlesBloom2020" class="citation journal cs1">Einav T, Gentles LE, Bloom JD (23 July 2020). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://github.com/TalEinav/InfluenzaSnapshot/blob/master/Cell%20Snapshot.pdf">"SnapShot: Influenza by the Numbers"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Cell</i>. <b>182</b> (2): 532. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/32707094">32707094</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Cell&amp;rft.atitle=SnapShot%3A+Influenza+by+the+Numbers&amp;rft.volume=182&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=532&amp;rft.date=2020-07-23&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F32707094&amp;rft.aulast=Einav&amp;rft.aufirst=T&amp;rft.au=Gentles%2C+LE&amp;rft.au=Bloom%2C+JD&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2FTalEinav%2FInfluenzaSnapshot%2Fblob%2Fmaster%2FCell%2520Snapshot.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AInfluenza" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008_26-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008_26-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008_26-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008_26-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFCarratVerguFergusonLemaitre2008" class="citation journal cs1">Carrat F, Vergu E, Ferguson NM, Lemaitre M, Cauchemez S, Leach S,  et&#160;al. </li>
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="Influenza#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See especially <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://academic.oup.com/view-large/figure/86199787/amjepidkwm375f05_lw.jpeg">Figure 5</a> which shows that virus shedding tends to peak on day 2 whereas symptoms tend to peak on day 3.</span>

<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="Influenza#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" Zarei, M; Idrovo, JP; Turner, RJ (9 October 2020). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/full/10.1002/rmv.2179">"Comparison of influenza type A and B with <li id="cite_note-WHOrecommendation-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-WHOrecommendation_126-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-WHOrecommendation_126-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.who.int/influenza/vaccines/2007northreport.pdf">"Recommended composition of influenza virus vaccines for use in the 2006–2007 influenza season"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <li id="cite_note-nfp:0-226"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="Influenza#cite_ref-nfp:0_226-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA64/A64_10-en.pdf">"Report of the Review Committee on the Functioning of the International Health Regulations (2005) in relation to Pandemic (H1N1) 2009"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. 5 May 2011. p.&#160;37. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150514145306/http://apps.who.int/gb/ebwha/pdf_files/WHA64/A64_10-en.pdf">Archived</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> from the original on 14 May 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. <p><b>Microbiology</b>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1004355016"/><div class="refbegin" style="">
<ul><li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFWebsterBeanGormanChambers1992" class="citation journal cs1">Webster RG, Bean WJ, Gorman OT, Chambers TM, Kawaoka Y (March 1992). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC372859">"Evolution and ecology of influenza A viruses"</a>. <i>Microbiological Reviews</i>. <b>56</b> (1): 152–79. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1128%2FMMBR.56.1.152-179.1992">10.1128/MMBR.56.1.152-179.1992</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a>&#160;<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC372859">372859</a></span>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/1579108">1579108</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Microbiological+Reviews&amp;rft.atitle=Evolution+and+ecology+of+influenza+A+viruses&amp;rft.volume=56&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=152-79&amp;rft.date=1992-03&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC372859%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F1579108&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1128%2FMMBR.56.1.152-179.1992&amp;rft.aulast=Webster&amp;rft.aufirst=RG&amp;rft.au=Bean%2C+WJ&amp;rft.au=Gorman%2C+OT&amp;rft.au=Chambers%2C+TM&amp;rft.au=Kawaoka%2C+Y&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC372859&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AInfluenza" class="Z3988"></span></li>
